Detailed Findings

AlertRiskURLDescriptionSolution
Missing Anti-clickjacking HeaderMediumhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/socket.io/?EIO=4&transport=polling&t=PC_hU2H&sid=75jt8A0Ck870Vq59AAJLThe response does not protect against 'ClickJacking' attacks. It should include either Content-Security-Policy with 'frame-ancestors' directive or X-Frame-Options.Modern Web browsers support the Content-Security-Policy and X-Frame-Options HTTP headers. Ensure one of them is set on all web pages returned by your site/app. If you expect the page to be framed only by pages on your server (e.g. it's part of a FRAMESET) then you'll want to use SAMEORIGIN, otherwise if you never expect the page to be framed, you should use DENY. Alternatively consider implementing Content Security Policy's "frame-ancestors" directive.
Timestamp Disclosure - UnixLowhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/socket.io/?EIO=4&transport=polling&t=PC_hToPA timestamp was disclosed by the application/web server. - UnixManually confirm that the timestamp data is not sensitive, and that the data cannot be aggregated to disclose exploitable patterns.
Content Security Policy (CSP) Header Not SetMediumhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/socket.io/?EIO=4&transport=polling&t=PC_hU2H&sid=75jt8A0Ck870Vq59AAJLContent Security Policy (CSP) is an added layer of security that helps to detect and mitigate certain types of attacks, including Cross Site Scripting (XSS) and data injection attacks. These attacks are used for everything from data theft to site defacement or distribution of malware. CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page — covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.
Session ID in URL RewriteMediumhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/socket.io/?EIO=4&transport=polling&t=PC_hU2H&sid=75jt8A0Ck870Vq59AAJLURL rewrite is used to track user session ID. The session ID may be disclosed via cross-site referer header. In addition, the session ID might be stored in browser history or server logs.For secure content, put session ID in a cookie. To be even more secure consider using a combination of cookie and URL rewrite.
X-Content-Type-Options Header MissingLowhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/socket.io/?EIO=4&transport=polling&t=PC_hToPThe Anti-MIME-Sniffing header X-Content-Type-Options was not set to 'nosniff'. This allows older versions of Internet Explorer and Chrome to perform MIME-sniffing on the response body, potentially causing the response body to be interpreted and displayed as a content type other than the declared content type. Current (early 2014) and legacy versions of Firefox will use the declared content type (if one is set), rather than performing MIME-sniffing.Ensure that the application/web server sets the Content-Type header appropriately, and that it sets the X-Content-Type-Options header to 'nosniff' for all web pages. If possible, ensure that the end user uses a standards-compliant and modern web browser that does not perform MIME-sniffing at all, or that can be directed by the web application/web server to not perform MIME-sniffing.

Missing Anti-clickjacking HeaderMediumhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/socket.io/?EIO=4&transport=polling&t=PC_hfeE&sid=c9koibrz1-BWj3ntAAKNThe response does not protect against 'ClickJacking' attacks. It should include either Content-Security-Policy with 'frame-ancestors' directive or X-Frame-Options.Modern Web browsers support the Content-Security-Policy and X-Frame-Options HTTP headers. Ensure one of them is set on all web pages returned by your site/app. If you expect the page to be framed only by pages on your server (e.g. it's part of a FRAMESET) then you'll want to use SAMEORIGIN, otherwise if you never expect the page to be framed, you should use DENY. Alternatively consider implementing Content Security Policy's "frame-ancestors" directive.

Content Security Policy (CSP) Header Not SetMediumhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/socket.io/?EIO=4&transport=polling&t=PC_hfeE&sid=c9koibrz1-BWj3ntAAKNContent Security Policy (CSP) is an added layer of security that helps to detect and mitigate certain types of attacks, including Cross Site Scripting (XSS) and data injection attacks. These attacks are used for everything from data theft to site defacement or distribution of malware. CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page — covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.

X-Content-Type-Options Header MissingLowhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/socket.io/?EIO=4&transport=polling&t=PC_hfeE&sid=c9koibrz1-BWj3ntAAKNThe Anti-MIME-Sniffing header X-Content-Type-Options was not set to 'nosniff'. This allows older versions of Internet Explorer and Chrome to perform MIME-sniffing on the response body, potentially causing the response body to be interpreted and displayed as a content type other than the declared content type. Current (early 2014) and legacy versions of Firefox will use the declared content type (if one is set), rather than performing MIME-sniffing.Ensure that the application/web server sets the Content-Type header appropriately, and that it sets the X-Content-Type-Options header to 'nosniff' for all web pages. If possible, ensure that the end user uses a standards-compliant and modern web browser that does not perform MIME-sniffing at all, or that can be directed by the web application/web server to not perform MIME-sniffing.

It should include either Content-Security-Policy with 'frame-ancestors' directive or X-Frame-Options.Modern Web browsers support the Content-Security-Policy and X-Frame-Options HTTP headers. Ensure one of them is set on all web pages returned by your site/app. If you expect the page to be framed only by pages on your server (e.g. it's part of a FRAMESET) then you'll want to use SAMEORIGIN, otherwise if you never expect the page to be framed, you should use DENY. Alternatively consider implementing Content Security Policy's "frame-ancestors" directive.
Content Security Policy (CSP) Header Not SetMediumhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/socket.io/?EIO=4&transport=polling&t=PC_i5jz&sid=5COK_edKEY8vAtwnAANHContent Security Policy (CSP) is an added layer of security that helps to detect and mitigate certain types of attacks, including Cross Site Scripting (XSS) and data injection attacks. These attacks are used for everything from data theft to site defacement or distribution of malware. CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page — covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.
Session ID in URL RewriteMediumhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/socket.io/?EIO=4&transport=polling&t=PC_i5jz&sid=5COK_edKEY8vAtwnAANHURL rewrite is used to track user session ID. The session ID may be disclosed via cross-site referer header. In addition, the session ID might be stored in browser history or server logs.For secure content, put session ID in a cookie. To be even more secure consider using a combination of cookie and URL rewrite.

X-Content-Type-Options Header MissingLowhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/socket.io/?EIO=4&transport=polling&t=PC_i5jz&sid=5COK_edKEY8vAtwnAANHThe Anti-MIME-Sniffing header X-Content-Type-Options was not set to 'nosniff'. This allows older versions of Internet Explorer and Chrome to perform MIME-sniffing on the response body, potentially causing the response body to be interpreted and displayed as a content type other than the declared content type. Current (early 2014) and legacy versions of Firefox will use the declared content type (if one is set), rather than performing MIME-sniffing.Ensure that the application/web server sets the Content-Type header appropriately, and that it sets the X-Content-Type-Options header to 'nosniff' for all web pages. If possible, ensure that the end user uses a standards-compliant and modern web browser that does not perform MIME-sniffing at all, or that can be directed by the web application/web server to not perform MIME-sniffing.

Application Error DisclosureLowhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/rest/products/1This page contains an error/warning message that may disclose sensitive information like the location of the file that produced the unhandled exception. This information can be used to launch further attacks against the web application. Content Security Policy (CSP) Header Not SetMediumhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/rest/products/1Content Security Policy (CSP) is an added layer of security that helps to detect and mitigate certain types of attacks, including Cross Site Scripting (XSS) and data injection attacks. These attacks are used for everything from data theft to site defacement or distribution of malware. CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page — covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.
Cross-Domain MisconfigurationMediumhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/rest/products/1Web browser data loading may be possible, due to a Cross Origin Resource Sharing (CORS) misconfiguration on the web server.Ensure that sensitive data is not available in an unauthenticated manner (using IP address white-listing, for instance). Configure the "Access-Control-Allow-Origin" HTTP header to a more restrictive set of domains, or remove all CORS headers entirely, to allow the web browser to enforce the Same Origin Policy (SOP) in a more restrictive manner.

Session ID in URL RewriteMediumhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/socket.io/?EIO=4&transport=polling&t=PC_hYzZ&sid=75jt8A0Ck870Vq59AAJLURL rewrite is used to track user session ID. The session ID may be disclosed via cross-site referer header. In addition, the session ID might be stored in browser history or server logs.For secure content, put session ID in a cookie. To be even more secure consider using a combination of cookie and URL rewrite.
Content Security Policy (CSP) Header Not SetMediumhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/apiContent Security Policy (CSP) is an added layer of security that helps to detect and mitigate certain types of attacks, including Cross Site Scripting (XSS) and data injection attacks. These attacks are used for everything from data theft to site defacement or distribution of malware. CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page — covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.

Content Security Policy (CSP) Header Not SetMediumhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/app/node_modules/express/lib/router/index.js:280:10Content Security Policy (CSP) is an added layer of security that helps to detect and mitigate certain types of attacks, including Cross Site Scripting (XSS) and data injection attacks. These attacks are used for everything from data theft to site defacement or distribution of malware. CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page — covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.

Configure the "Access-Control-Allow-Origin" HTTP header to a more restrictive set of domains, or remove all CORS headers entirely, to allow the web browser to enforce the Same Origin Policy (SOP) in a more restrictive manner.

Content Security Policy (CSP) Header Not SetMediumhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/app/node_modules/express/lib/router/assets/public/favicon_js.icoContent Security Policy (CSP) is an added layer of security that helps to detect and mitigate certain types of attacks, including Cross Site Scripting (XSS) and data injection attacks. These attacks are used for everything from data theft to site defacement or distribution of malware. CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page — covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.
Cross-Domain MisconfigurationMediumhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/assets/public/images/products/runtime.jsWeb browser data loading may be possible, due to a Cross Origin Resource Sharing (CORS) misconfiguration on the web server.Ensure that sensitive data is not available in an unauthenticated manner (using IP address white-listing, for instance). Configure the "Access-Control-Allow-Origin" HTTP header to a more restrictive set of domains, or remove all CORS headers entirely, to allow the web browser to enforce the Same Origin Policy (SOP) in a more restrictive manner.

Content Security Policy (CSP) Header Not SetMediumhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/app/build/routes/vendor.jsContent Security Policy (CSP) is an added layer of security that helps to detect and mitigate certain types of attacks, including Cross Site Scripting (XSS) and data injection attacks. These attacks are used for everything from data theft to site defacement or distribution of malware. CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page — covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.
Timestamp Disclosure - UnixLowhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/app/build/routes/styles.cssA timestamp was disclosed by the application/web server. - UnixManually confirm that the timestamp data is not sensitive, and that the data cannot be aggregated to disclose exploitable patterns.
Cross-Domain MisconfigurationMediumhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/app/build/routes/vendor.jsWeb browser data loading may be possible, due to a Cross Origin Resource Sharing (CORS) misconfiguration on the web server.Ensure that sensitive data is not available in an unauthenticated manner (using IP address white-listing, for instance). Configure the "Access-Control-Allow-Origin" HTTP header to a more restrictive set of domains, or remove all CORS headers entirely, to allow the web browser to enforce the Same Origin Policy (SOP) in a more restrictive manner.

CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page — covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.
Cross-Domain JavaScript Source File InclusionLowhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/app/node_modules/morgan/assets/public/favicon_js.icoThe page includes one or more script files from a third-party domain.Ensure JavaScript source files are loaded from only trusted sources, and the sources can't be controlled by end users of the application.
Cross-Domain MisconfigurationMediumhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/app/node_modules/morgan/runtime.jsWeb browser data loading may be possible, due to a Cross Origin Resource Sharing (CORS) misconfiguration on the web server.Ensure that sensitive data is not available in an unauthenticated manner (using IP address white-listing, for instance). Configure the "Access-Control-Allow-Origin" HTTP header to a more restrictive set of domains, or remove all CORS headers entirely, to allow the web browser to enforce the Same Origin Policy (SOP) in a more restrictive manner.

Content Security Policy (CSP) Header Not SetMediumhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/assets/assets/public/assets/public/favicon_js.icoContent Security Policy (CSP) is an added layer of security that helps to detect and mitigate certain types of attacks, including Cross Site Scripting (XSS) and data injection attacks. These attacks are used for everything from data theft to site defacement or distribution of malware. CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page — covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.

Content Security Policy (CSP) Header Not SetMediumhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/app/node_modules/express/lib/router/assets/public/assets/public/favicon_js.icoContent Security Policy (CSP) is an added layer of security that helps to detect and mitigate certain types of attacks, including Cross Site Scripting (XSS) and data injection attacks. These attacks are used for everything from data theft to site defacement or distribution of malware. CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page — covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.
Cross-Domain MisconfigurationMediumhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/app/node_modules/express/lib/router/assets/public/assets/public/favicon_js.icoWeb browser data loading may be possible, due to a Cross Origin Resource Sharing (CORS) misconfiguration on the web server.Ensure that sensitive data is not available in an unauthenticated manner (using IP address white-listing, for instance). Configure the "Access-Control-Allow-Origin" HTTP header to a more restrictive set of domains, or remove all CORS headers entirely, to allow the web browser to enforce the Same Origin Policy (SOP) in a more restrictive manner.

Content Security Policy (CSP) Header Not SetMediumhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/app/node_modules/express/lib/router/assets/public/polyfills.jsContent Security Policy (CSP) is an added layer of security that helps to detect and mitigate certain types of attacks, including Cross Site Scripting (XSS) and data injection attacks. These attacks are used for everything from data theft to site defacement or distribution of malware. CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page — covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.
Cross-Domain MisconfigurationMediumhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/app/node_modules/express/lib/router/assets/public/polyfills.jsWeb browser data loading may be possible, due to a Cross Origin Resource Sharing (CORS) misconfiguration on the web server.Ensure that sensitive data is not available in an unauthenticated manner (using IP address white-listing, for instance). Configure the "Access-Control-Allow-Origin" HTTP header to a more restrictive set of domains, or remove all CORS headers entirely, to allow the web browser to enforce the Same Origin Policy (SOP) in a more restrictive manner.

Content Security Policy (CSP) Header Not SetMediumhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/assets/public/images/assets/public/assets/public/styles.cssContent Security Policy (CSP) is an added layer of security that helps to detect and mitigate certain types of attacks, including Cross Site Scripting (XSS) and data injection attacks. These attacks are used for everything from data theft to site defacement or distribution of malware. CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page — covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.

Cross-Domain MisconfigurationMediumhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/assets/public/images/assets/public/assets/public/styles.cssWeb browser data loading may be possible, due to a Cross Origin Resource Sharing (CORS) misconfiguration on the web server.Ensure that sensitive data is not available in an unauthenticated manner (using IP address white-listing, for instance). Configure the "Access-Control-Allow-Origin" HTTP header to a more restrictive set of domains, or remove all CORS headers entirely, to allow the web browser to enforce the Same Origin Policy (SOP) in a more restrictive manner.

Cross-Domain MisconfigurationMediumhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/assets/public/assets/public/assets/public/main.jsWeb browser data loading may be possible, due to a Cross Origin Resource Sharing (CORS) misconfiguration on the web server.Ensure that sensitive data is not available in an unauthenticated manner (using IP address white-listing, for instance). Configure the "Access-Control-Allow-Origin" HTTP header to a more restrictive set of domains, or remove all CORS headers entirely, to allow the web browser to enforce the Same Origin Policy (SOP) in a more restrictive manner.

Content Security Policy (CSP) Header Not SetMediumhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/app/node_modules/express/lib/router/assets/public/assets/public/assets/public/assets/public/favicon_js.icoContent Security Policy (CSP) is an added layer of security that helps to detect and mitigate certain types of attacks, including Cross Site Scripting (XSS) and data injection attacks. These attacks are used for everything from data theft to site defacement or distribution of malware. CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page — covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.

Cross-Domain MisconfigurationMediumhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/app/node_modules/express/lib/router/assets/public/assets/public/assets/public/assets/public/favicon_js.icoWeb browser data loading may be possible, due to a Cross Origin Resource Sharing (CORS) misconfiguration on the web server.Ensure that sensitive data is not available in an unauthenticated manner (using IP address white-listing, for instance). Configure the "Access-Control-Allow-Origin" HTTP header to a more restrictive set of domains, or remove all CORS headers entirely, to allow the web browser to enforce the Same Origin Policy (SOP) in a more restrictive manner.

CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page — covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.
Cross-Domain MisconfigurationMediumhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/assets/assets/public/assets/public/assets/public/main.jsWeb browser data loading may be possible, due to a Cross Origin Resource Sharing (CORS) misconfiguration on the web server.Ensure that sensitive data is not available in an unauthenticated manner (using IP address white-listing, for instance). Configure the "Access-Control-Allow-Origin" HTTP header to a more restrictive set of domains, or remove all CORS headers entirely, to allow the web browser to enforce the Same Origin Policy (SOP) in a more restrictive manner.

Content Security Policy (CSP) Header Not SetMediumhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/assets/public/assets/public/assets/public/assets/public/polyfills.jsContent Security Policy (CSP) is an added layer of security that helps to detect and mitigate certain types of attacks, including Cross Site Scripting (XSS) and data injection attacks. These attacks are used for everything from data theft to site defacement or distribution of malware. CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page — covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.

Re-examine Cache-control DirectivesInformationalhttps://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/The cache-control header has not been set properly or is missing, allowing the browser and proxies to cache content. For static assets like css, js, or image files this might be intended, however, the resources should be reviewed to ensure that no sensitive content will be cached.For secure content, ensure the cache-control HTTP header is set with "no-cache, no-store, must-revalidate". If an asset should be cached consider setting the directives "public, max-age, immutable".

Strict-Transport-Security Header Not SetLowhttps://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/polyfills.jsHTTP Strict Transport Security (HSTS) is a web security policy mechanism whereby a web server declares that complying user agents (such as a web browser) are to interact with it using only secure HTTPS connections (i.e. HTTP layered over TLS/SSL). HSTS is an IETF standards track protocol and is specified in RFC 6797.Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to enforce Strict-Transport-Security.

SQL Injection - SQLiteHighhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/rest/products/search?q=%27%28SQL injection may be possible.Do not trust client side input, even if there is client side validation in place. In general, type check all data on the server side. If the application uses JDBC, use PreparedStatement or CallableStatement, with parameters passed by '?' If the application uses ASP, use ADO Command Objects with strong type checking and parameterized queries. If database Stored Procedures can be used, use them. Do *not* concatenate strings into queries in the stored procedure, or use 'exec', 'exec immediate', or equivalent functionality! Do not create dynamic SQL queries using simple string concatenation. Escape all data received from the client. Apply an 'allow list' of allowed characters, or a 'deny list' of disallowed characters in user input. Apply the principle of least privilege by using the least privileged database user possible. In particular, avoid using the 'sa' or 'db-owner' database users. This does not eliminate SQL injection, but minimizes its impact. Grant the minimum database access that is necessary for the application.
Timestamp Disclosure - UnixLowhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/socket.io/?EIO=4&transport=polling&t=PC_iejFA timestamp was disclosed by the application/web server. - UnixManually confirm that the timestamp data is not sensitive, and that the data cannot be aggregated to disclose exploitable patterns.
X-Content-Type-Options Header MissingLowhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/socket.io/?EIO=4&transport=polling&t=PC_iejFThe Anti-MIME-Sniffing header X-Content-Type-Options was not set to 'nosniff'. This allows older versions of Internet Explorer and Chrome to perform MIME-sniffing on the response body, potentially causing the response body to be interpreted and displayed as a content type other than the declared content type. Current (early 2014) and legacy versions of Firefox will use the declared content type (if one is set), rather than performing MIME-sniffing.Ensure that the application/web server sets the Content-Type header appropriately, and that it sets the X-Content-Type-Options header to 'nosniff' for all web pages. If possible, ensure that the end user uses a standards-compliant and modern web browser that does not perform MIME-sniffing at all, or that can be directed by the web application/web server to not perform MIME-sniffing.
Missing Anti-clickjacking HeaderMediumhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/socket.io/?EIO=4&transport=polling&t=PC_if5A&sid=c50Yb0SuJ2f-pbNOAAVTThe response does not protect against 'ClickJacking' attacks. It should include either Content-Security-Policy with 'frame-ancestors' directive or X-Frame-Options.Modern Web browsers support the Content-Security-Policy and X-Frame-Options HTTP headers. Ensure one of them is set on all web pages returned by your site/app. If you expect the page to be framed only by pages on your server (e.g. it's part of a FRAMESET) then you'll want to use SAMEORIGIN, otherwise if you never expect the page to be framed, you should use DENY. Alternatively consider implementing Content Security Policy's "frame-ancestors" directive.
Content Security Policy (CSP) Header Not SetMediumhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/socket.io/?EIO=4&transport=polling&t=PC_if5A&sid=c50Yb0SuJ2f-pbNOAAVTContent Security Policy (CSP) is an added layer of security that helps to detect and mitigate certain types of attacks, including Cross Site Scripting (XSS) and data injection attacks. These attacks are used for everything from data theft to site defacement or distribution of malware. CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page — covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.
Session ID in URL RewriteMediumhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/socket.io/?EIO=4&transport=polling&t=PC_if5A&sid=c50Yb0SuJ2f-pbNOAAVTURL rewrite is used to track user session ID. The session ID may be disclosed via cross-site referer header. In addition, the session ID might be stored in browser history or server logs.For secure content, put session ID in a cookie. To be even more secure consider using a combination of cookie and URL rewrite.

X-Content-Type-Options Header MissingLowhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/socket.io/?EIO=4&transport=polling&t=PC_ixs1The Anti-MIME-Sniffing header X-Content-Type-Options was not set to 'nosniff'. This allows older versions of Internet Explorer and Chrome to perform MIME-sniffing on the response body, potentially causing the response body to be interpreted and displayed as a content type other than the declared content type. Current (early 2014) and legacy versions of Firefox will use the declared content type (if one is set), rather than performing MIME-sniffing.Ensure that the application/web server sets the Content-Type header appropriately, and that it sets the X-Content-Type-Options header to 'nosniff' for all web pages. If possible, ensure that the end user uses a standards-compliant and modern web browser that does not perform MIME-sniffing at all, or that can be directed by the web application/web server to not perform MIME-sniffing.

Session ID in URL RewriteMediumhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/socket.io/?EIO=4&transport=websocket&sid=i-6ePZ6rYIY3O3LIAAXYURL rewrite is used to track user session ID. Missing Anti-clickjacking HeaderMediumhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/socket.io/?EIO=4&transport=polling&t=PC_ixtv&sid=i-6ePZ6rYIY3O3LIAAXYThe response does not protect against 'ClickJacking' attacks. It should include either Content-Security-Policy with 'frame-ancestors' directive or X-Frame-Options.Modern Web browsers support the Content-Security-Policy and X-Frame-Options HTTP headers. Ensure one of them is set on all web pages returned by your site/app. If you expect the page to be framed only by pages on your server (e.g. it's part of a FRAMESET) then you'll want to use SAMEORIGIN, otherwise if you never expect the page to be framed, you should use DENY. Alternatively consider implementing Content Security Policy's "frame-ancestors" directive.

Content Security Policy (CSP) Header Not SetMediumhttp://juice-shop.herokuapp.com/socket.io/?EIO=4&transport=polling&t=PC_ixtv&sid=i-6ePZ6rYIY3O3LIAAXYContent Security Policy (CSP) is an added layer of security that helps to detect and mitigate certain types of attacks, including Cross Site Scripting (XSS) and data injection attacks. These attacks are used for everything from data theft to site defacement or distribution of malware. CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page — covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.

The session ID may be disclosed via cross-site referer header. In addition, the session ID might be stored in browser history or server logs.For secure content, put session ID in a cookie. To be even more secure consider using a combination of cookie and URL rewrite.
